ولا يستحلف في نكاح ورجعة وفيء واستيلاد ورق ونسب وولاء وحد ولعان، أي المدعى عليه في نكاح مجرد عن المال عند أبي حنيفة، أما إذا ادعت المرأة أنه تزوجها على كذا، أو ادعت النفقة وأنكر الزوج، فحينئذ يستحلف ورجعة أي بعد العدة، فإنه إذا ادعى الرجعة في العدة تثبت بقوله "وإن كذبته؛ لأنه ادعى أمراً يملك استينافه للحال. وفيء: أي فيء الإيلاء بعد مضي مدتها، ولو ادعى الفيء في مدة الإيلاء ثبت بقوله. واستيلاد: بأن ادعت أمة على سيدها أنها ولدت منه هذا الولد، أو ولداً قد مات، وأنكر السيد، ولا يتأتى من الجانب الآخر؛ إذ لو ادعى المولى يثبت الاستيلاد بإقراره ولا يعتبر إنكارها، وكذا الحد واللعان، بخلاف سائر الأشياء المذكورة؛ إذ يتأتى فيها الدعوى من الجانبين وفي الحد واللعان لا يتصور أن يكون المدعي إلا المقذوف وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة، وإنما لا يحلف في الأشياء الستة عنده؛ لأن النكول بذل وإباحة والبذل قطع الخصومة بدفع ما يدعيه الخصم، وقيل: ترك المنع أي المنازعة، والإعراض عنها؛ إذ لو حمل النكول على الإقرار لكذبناه في الإنكار، ولو جعل بذلاً انقطعت الخصومة بلا تكذيب فكان هذا أولى صيانة للمسلم عن أن يظن به الكذب، وهذه حقوق لا يجري فيها البذل، فلا يقضى فيها بالنكول كالقصاص في النفس بخلاف الأموال. والحاصل أن كل محل يقبل الإباحة بالإذن ابتداء يقضى عليه بنكوله، ومالا فلا. لا يقال: إن أبا حنيفة ترك الحديث المشهور، وهو قوله علي واليمين على من أنكر" بالرأي، وهو لا يجوز؛ لأنه لم ينف وجوب اليمين فيها، لكنه يقول: لما لم تفد اليمين فائدتها. القضاء بالنكول؛ لكونه بذلاً لا يجري فيها وهو سقطت كسقوط الوجوب عن معذور لا يتحقق منه أداء الصلاة؛ لفوات المقصود، وقالا يستحلف فيها؛ لأن النكول كالإقرار، والقضاء بالإقرار جائز، فكذا بالنكول كما في الأموال، وبه قالت الثلاثة وبه يفتى، وكان ينبغي هنا أن يقال: "في نكاح مجرد عن المال" يعني إذا لم يكن المقصود هو المال، فأما إذا كان المقصود هو المال كما إذا ادعت امرأة على رجل أنه تزوجها بألف وطلقها قبل الدخول بها، ولها عليه نصف المهر، فإنه يستحلف بالإجماع، فإن نكل قضى عليه بنصف المهر. (عيني، فتح) ورق بأن ادعى على مجهول النسب أنه عبده وهو يجحد أو بالعكس. (عيني) ونسب: بأن ادعى على مجهول النسب أنه ابنه وأنكر الآخر، أو بالعكس. (عيني) وولاء : بأن ادعى على معروف النسب أنه معتقه وأنكر الآخر، أو بالعكس، أو كان ذلك في ولاء الموالاة. (عيني) وحد ولعان أي ولا يستحلف في حد بأن ادعى على آخر أنك قد قذفتني بالزنا وعليك الحد، وهو ينكر ، وكذا لا يستحلف في لعان بأن ادعت امرأة على زوجها أنه قذفها بالزنا، وعليه اللعان، وهو منكر، ففي الصورتين لا يستحلف إجماعاً إلا إذا تضمن حقاً بأن علق عتق عبده بالزنا - أي زنا نفسه - وقال: إن زنيت فأنت حر، فادعى العبد أنه قد زنى ولا بينة للعبد عليه، استحلف المولى، حتى إذا نكل يثبت العتق دون الزنا، وإنما لا يستحلف في الحد؛ لأنه يندرئ بالشبهات وفي اللعان؛ لأنه في معنى وقالوا: إنه يستحلف في التعزير؛ لأنه في حكم الأموال، ولذلك يصح فيه العفو والإبراء. (عيني، فتح) وهو من قيد الحد، قال القاضي الإمام فخر الدين له الفتوى على أنه يستحلف المنكر في الأشياء الستة، ويستحلف السارق، فإن نكل ،ضمن ولم يقطع، والزوج إذا ادعت المرأة قاضي أي السارق عن اليمين الإمام فخر الدين حسن بن منصور بن أبي القاسم محمود بن عبد العزيز الأوزجندي الفرغاني المعروف خان صاحب الفتاوى، تفقه على جماعة من الكبار منهم : أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن علي المرغيناني، وتفقه عليه جماعة من الكبار، منهم: شمس الأئمة محمد بن عبد الستار الكردري، توفي يوم الاثنين خامس عشر رمضان سنة خمس مائة واثنين وتسعين رحمه الله. [رمز الحقائق: ١٩٠/٢] الأشياء الستة والحاصل أن المفتى به التحليف في الكل إلا في الحدود. (ط)] وهي النكاح والرجعة والفيء والرق والنسب والولاء. فإن قلت المذكور تسعة أشياء؟ قلت: قد ذكرنا أن عدم التحليف في الحد واللعان مجمع عليه، فبقيت سبعة، والاستيلاد ملحق بالستة؛ لأن الدعوى فيه دعوى النسب أو دعوى الرق، فتبقى الستة، وهي المختلفة فيها بين الإمام وصاحبيه، واختار الإمام علي البزدوي أيضاً قولهما مثل ما نص عليه القاضي خان، واختار بعض المتأخرين أن القاضي ينظر في حال المدعى عليه، فإن رآه متعنتاً يحلفه آخذاً بقولهما، وإن رآه مظلوماً لا يحلفه آخذاً بقول أبي حنيفة لله [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۹۰/۲] وصورة الاستحلاف على قولهما في النكاح مثلا: ما بزوجة لي وإن كانت زوجة لي فهي طالق بائن؛ لأنها لو كانت صادقة لا يبطل النكاح بجحوده فإذا حلف تبقى معطلة، وقال بعضهم: يستحلف على النكاح فإن حلف بقول القاضي فرقت بينهما. (فتح)
And the defendant is not sworn in [cases of] marriage, return (raj'a), fay' (return to intercourse after ila'), istilad (claiming a child from a slave woman), slavery, lineage, clientage (wala'), hadd (fixed punishment), and li'an (imprecation). That is, the defendant is not sworn in marriage purely without property according to Abu Hanifa. However, if the woman claims that he married her for a certain amount, or claims maintenance and the husband denies, then he is sworn. And raj'a: that is, after the waiting period, because if he claims raj'a during the waiting period it is established by his statement even if she denies him, because he claims a matter that he can initiate at present. And fay': that is, fay' of ila' after the expiry of its period; if he claims fay' during the period of ila' it is established by his statement. And istilad: when a slave woman claims against her master that she gave birth to this child from him, or a child who died, and the master denies, and it does not occur from the other side; because if the master claimed it, istilad is established by his acknowledgment and her denial is not considered. Similarly, hadd and li'an, unlike the other mentioned matters because in them the claim can be from both sides, while in hadd and li'an the claimant can only be the person who was slandered. All this is according to Abu Hanifa. The reason he does not make the defendant swear in the six matters is that nukul (refusal to swear) is a concession (bazl) and permission, and concession cuts the dispute by giving what the opponent claims. It is said: it is abandoning the objection (al-man') and turning away from it; because if nukul were treated as confession we would be accusing him of lying in his denial, but if it is made a concession the dispute ends without accusation of lying, and this is more appropriate to protect a Muslim from being suspected of lying. And these are rights in which concession (bazl) does not apply, so judgment is not given by nukul, like qisas for life, unlike property. In summary: every context that originally accepts permission by consent, judgment is given against him by his nukul, and what does not accept it, not. It cannot be said that Abu Hanifa abandoned the famous hadith, which is his statement 'The oath is on the one who denies' by opinion, and that is not permissible; because he did not deny the obligation of the oath in them, but he says: since the oath does not achieve its benefit (of judgment by nukul because it is a concession that does not apply in these matters), it falls like the obligation falling for one who is excused and cannot perform prayer because the objective is lost. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is sworn in these matters because nukul is like confession, and judgment by confession is permissible, so too by nukul as in property. And the three (other schools) say this, and according to this fatwa is given. It should have been said here: 'in marriage free from property' meaning when the objective is not property. But when the objective is property, as when a woman claims that a man married her for a thousand and divorced her before consummation, and she has a claim for half the dower, then he is sworn by consensus; if he refuses, judgment is given for half the dower. ('Ayni, Fath) And slavery: when someone claims of a person of unknown lineage that he is his slave and he denies, or vice versa. ('Ayni) And lineage: when someone claims of a person of unknown lineage that he is his son and the other denies, or vice versa. ('Ayni) And clientage (wala'): when someone claims of a person of known lineage that he is his emancipator and the other denies, or vice versa, or in clientage of alliance. ('Ayni) And hadd and li'an: the defendant is not sworn in hadd when one claims against another that you slandered me of adultery and upon you is the hadd, and he denies; similarly, he is not sworn in li'an when a woman claims against her husband that he slandered her of adultery and upon him is li'an, and he denies. In both cases he is not sworn by consensus, except if it includes a right, such as when he conditioned the emancipation of his slave on his own adultery and said: 'If I commit adultery, you are free,' and the slave claims that he committed adultery and there is no evidence for the slave, then the master is sworn, and if he refuses, the emancipation is established without the adultery. The reason he is not sworn in hadd is that it is repelled by doubts; and in li'an because it is similar. And they said: he is sworn in ta'zir (discretionary punishment) because it is like property matters, therefore forgiveness and release are valid in it. ('Ayni, Fath) This is from the restriction of hadd. The judge, Imam Fakhr al-Din, said: the fatwa is that the defendant is sworn in the six matters, and the thief is sworn, and if he refuses he is liable but not cut, and the husband when the woman claims... The judge, that is, regarding the thief's oath. Imam Fakhr al-Din Hasan ibn Mansur ibn Abi al-Qasim Mahmud ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Uzjandi al-Farghani, known as Khan Sahib al-Fatawa, studied under a group of great scholars including Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Marghinani, and many great scholars studied under him, including Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari. He died on Monday, the fifteenth of Ramadan, in the year five hundred and ninety-two, may Allah have mercy on him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:190] The six matters: the summary is that the mufta bihi is requiring the oath in all except hadd. (T) They are: marriage, return, fay', slavery, lineage, and clientage. If you say: nine things were mentioned? I say: we mentioned that the absence of the oath in hadd and li'an is agreed upon, so seven remain, and istilad is attached to the six because the claim in it is a claim of lineage or a claim of slavery, so six remain, which are the matters of difference between the Imam and his two companions. Imam 'Ali al-Bazdawi also chose their statement as stated by Qadi Khan, and some later scholars chose that the judge looks at the situation of the defendant; if he sees him as obstinate he swears him, taking from their statement, and if he sees him as oppressed he does not swear him, taking from Abu Hanifa's statement for Allah. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:190] The form of swearing according to their statement in marriage, for example: 'I have no wife, and if I have a wife, she is divorced with a final divorce'; because if she were truthful, the marriage would not be invalidated by his denial, so if he swears she remains suspended. Some said: he is sworn regarding the marriage, and if he swears, according to the judge's opinion, he separates between them. (Fath)
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary discusses the procedural ruling of whether a defendant (munkar) is required to take an oath (yastahlif) in certain types of claims. The text begins by stating the general rule according to Imam Abu Hanifa: the defendant is not sworn in six specific matters—marriage (nikah), return (raj'a), return to intercourse after ila' (fay'), claiming a child from a slave woman (istilad), slavery (riqq), lineage (nasab), and clientage (wala'). Additionally, hadd (fixed punishment) and li'an (imprecation) are excluded by consensus. The commentary explains that this rule applies when the claim is free from property considerations. If property is involved, such as when the woman claims dower or maintenance, the defendant is sworn even in these matters, by consensus. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's position is that nukul (refusal to swear) is treated as a concession (bazl) to end the dispute, not as a confession (iqrar). In these non-property rights, concession does not apply, so nukul cannot be the basis for a judgment. The famous hadith 'The oath is on the one who denies' is not rejected; rather, its benefit is not realized in these cases because the purpose of the oath is to enable judgment by nukul, which is not applicable. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that nukul is equivalent to confession, so judgment can be given based on it, as in property cases. The three other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) agree with the companions, and the fatwa is given accordingly, except in hadd. The passage then provides examples and further details, including the view of Qadi Fakhr al-Din that the reliance (mufta bihi) is to require the oath in all six matters except hadd. Some later scholars allow the judge discretion based on the defendant's attitude. The biographical note on Qadi Fakhr al-Din confirms his authority. The lesson encapsulates a key intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute with practical implications.

Key Terms
نكول (nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take an oath after being asked by the judge.
بذل (bazl): Concession by the defendant to end the dispute by giving what the claimant demands, interpreted from nukul.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission by a party that can be used as evidence for judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the legal classification of nukul (defendant's refusal to swear)?
A) It is equivalent to confession (iqrar) and leads to judgment.
B) It is a concession (bazl) to end the dispute, applicable only in property matters.
C) It is ignored; the judge proceeds without any effect.
D) It results in dismissal of the case.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's internal dispute on nukul — bazl vs iqrar — produces different procedural outcomes; the relied-upon position requires the oath in all claims except hadd.

Swearing the Thief and Husband in Property Claims
Rulings on swearing the thief and husband in property claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a thief and a husband are sworn in property claims and explain the consequence of nukul.

Core Idea
Nukul establishes monetary liability but not hadd or personal status.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentaries clarifies the application of oaths in two specific cases: the accused thief and the husband. It demonstrates a key Hanafi principle: nukul (refusal to swear) suffices for financial claims but not for fixed punishments or marital bonds. The reasoning (ta'lil) hinges on the difference between matters proven by weak evidence and those requiring certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parties discussed
The thief (sariq) and the husband (zawj). Each has specific conditions for swearing.
2
Analyze the thief's oath
The thief is sworn only when the victim's aim is to recover the money, not to enforce the hadd. The oath formula is given. If he refuses (nukul), he becomes liable for the money, but his hand is not cut.
Reason: hadd punishments require stronger evidence; nukul is only sufficient for property.
3
Understand the husband's oath
The husband is sworn when the wife claims dower or maintenance during the waiting period. Nukul establishes the monetary claim but not the marriage itself.
The marriage (nikah) cannot be established by nukul because it requires certainty.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
Property claims (daman) can be proven by weak evidence (shubah), so nukul suffices. Hadd punishments and personal status require higher evidentiary standards.
This is a consistent theme in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحلف السارق قيد بحد السرقة؛ لأن غيره من بقية الحدود لا يستحلف فيها بالإجماع. ويستحلف السارق إذا كان مراد المسروق منه أخذ المال بأن يقول : بالله ما له عليك هذا المال. فإن نكل ضمن: أي امتنع عن اليمين ضمن المال؛ لأنه يثبت بالشبهات فجاز أن يثبت بالنكول. هي ولم يقطع [أي يد السارق وإن أقر قطع. (ط) (معدن)] لأن المنوط بفعله شيئان: الضمان ويعمل فيه بالنكول، والقطع وهو لا يثبت بالنكول فصار كما إذا شهد على السرقة رجل وامرأتان فيقضى بشهادة الرجل والمرأتين بالنسبة لضمان المال دون القطع؛ لأن الحجة مشتمل على الشبهة، وعن محمد أنه قال: يقول القاضي المدعي: ماذا تريد؟ فإن قال: أريد القطع، يقول له: الحدود لا يستحلف فيها فليس لك يمين وإن قال: أريد المال يقول له: دع دعوى السرقة وانبعث على دعوى المال. (عناية، فتح) والزوج بالرفع عطف على السارق أي ويستحلف الزوج. (عيني) إذا ادعت المرأة: ولا فرق بين " أن المهر أو نفقة العدة والتقييد قبل الوطء اتفاقي لكن فائدة تعيين صورة المسألة فى الطلاق قبل الوطء: هي . دعوى المهر لا تتفاوت بين أن تكون الدعوى في كل المهر أو نصفه وسواء كان دعوى المهر في صورة الطلاق أو لا، والاستحلاف يجري في الطلاق بالإجماع، وكذا في النكاح إذا ادعت الصداق أو النفقة؛ لأنه دعوى المال، ثم يثبت المال بنكوله، ولا يثبت النكاح. (فتح) أن تدعي تعليم
And the thief is sworn, restricted to the hadd of theft because other hadd punishments are not sworn by consensus. The thief is sworn when the victim's aim is to take the money, by saying: 'By Allah, you are not owed this money.' If he refuses, he is liable: that is, if he abstains from the oath he becomes liable for the money because [the money] can be established by doubts, so it is permissible to establish it by nukul. And the hand is not cut, even if he confesses it is cut. (T, Ma'din) Because two things are attached to his act: liability (daman) which is acted upon by nukul, and amputation (qat') which is not established by nukul. So it is like when a man and two women testify to theft: judgment is given based on their testimony regarding monetary liability but not amputation because the evidence contains doubt. And from Muhammad that he said: The judge says to the claimant: 'What do you want?' If he says: 'I want amputation,' he says: 'Hadd punishments are not sworn in, so you have no oath.' If he says: 'I want the money,' he says: 'Leave the claim of theft and proceed on the claim of money.' ('Inaya, Fath) And 'al-zawj' (the husband) is nominative, coordinated with 'al-sariq', meaning the husband is also sworn. ('Ayni) When the woman claims: and there is no difference between [claiming] the dower or the maintenance of the waiting period, and the restriction to before consummation is by convention, but the benefit of specifying the form of the issue in divorce before consummation is that the claim of dower does not vary whether the claim is for the entire dower or half, and it is the same whether the claim of dower is in the context of divorce or not. The oath is applicable in divorce by consensus, and likewise in marriage if she claims the dower or maintenance because it is a claim for property; then the property is established by his nukul, but the marriage is not established. (Fath) ...that you claim... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on swearing in legal proceedings, focusing on two specific cases: the thief (sariq) and the husband (zawj). It begins by stating that the thief is sworn only in the context of the hadd of theft (sarqa); other hadd punishments are not sworn by consensus. The thief is sworn when the victim's objective is to recover the stolen money, not to enforce the hadd amputation. The oath formula is: 'By Allah, you are not owed this money.' If the thief refuses to swear (nukul), he becomes liable for the money because monetary claims can be established even on the basis of doubts (shubuhat), and nukul is treated as a basis for liability in property matters. However, the hand amputation (qat') is not imposed based on nukul because hadd punishments are repelled by doubts and cannot be established through nukul. An analogy is drawn with testimony: if a man and two women witness theft, judgment is given for the money but not for amputation because the evidence contains doubt. Imam Muhammad adds that the judge should ask the claimant what he wants—if he seeks amputation, he is told no oath is available; if he seeks money, the claim is treated as a property claim. Then, the husband (zawj) is also sworn in certain cases. Specifically, if the wife claims dower (mahr) or maintenance during the waiting period (nafaqat al-idda), the husband is sworn. This applies whether the claim is in the context of divorce or marriage, by consensus. If the husband refuses to swear, the property (dower or maintenance) is established, but the marriage itself is not established by nukul. The passage highlights the Hanafi principle that nukul can establish property rights but not personal status or hadd punishments.

Key Terms
حد السرقة (hadd al-sariqa): The fixed punishment for theft: amputation of the hand.
ضمان (daman): Liability for monetary compensation, established by nukul in property claims.
قطع (qat'): Amputation of the hand as the hadd punishment for theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the thief refuses to swear (nukul) regarding a theft claim?
A) Both liability for the money and hand amputation are imposed.
B) Liability for the money is imposed, but hand amputation is not.
C) Hand amputation is imposed, but liability for the money is not.
D) The case is dismissed entirely.

Key Takeaway
Nukul (refusal to swear) in Hanafi fiqh establishes monetary liability but not hadd punishments or personal status, reflecting the principle that property claims require lower evidentiary certainty.

Oath for the Six Categories of Claims
States the fatwa on administering oath in six specific claims, with intra-madhhab disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six categories in which the denier is made to swear an oath according to the Hanafi mufta bihi, and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The Hanafi mufta bihi administers oaths only in six specific claims, excluding hudud and li'an.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi rule: the denier (al-munkir) is made to swear an oath only in six specific categories of claims, not in all lawsuits. The passage from Qadi Khan's Fatawa clarifies the mufta bihi position (Sahibayn's view) and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Imam Abu Hanifa. Understanding this topic is essential for a judge or mufti handling legal claims in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine what the mufta bihi ruling is regarding administering oaths to the denier. Note that it applies only in certain claims and not in hudud or li'an.
The ruling is that the denier is made to swear an oath in six specific categories.
2
List the six categories
Name the six categories: marriage (nikah), revocation (raj'ah), return (fay'), slavery (riq), lineage (nasab), and patronage (wala'). Understand why istilad (claim of umm walad) is attached to the six.
The passage explains that istilad is subsumed under slavery or lineage.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab disagreement
Identify the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa (no oath) and the Sahibayn (oath administered). Examine the evidence each uses: Abu Hanifa's concern about harm from false oaths vs. the Sahibayn's reliance on the hadith 'lak yaminuhu' and istihsan.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
4
Understand the practical implementation
Study the example given for marriage: the oath is phrased with a conditional divorce so that a false oath instantly dissolves the marriage. This protects the plaintiff and is a form of istihsan.
This conditional formula is key to the Sahibayn's justification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الدعوى
كتاب الدعوى
قال القاضي الإمام فخر الدين له الفتوى على أنه يستحلف المنكر في الأشياء
القاضي
الستة، ويستحلف السارق، فإن نكل ،ضمن ولم يقطع، والزوج إذا ادعت المرأة
قاضي
أي السارق عن اليمين
الإمام فخر الدين حسن بن منصور بن أبي القاسم محمود بن عبد العزيز الأوزجندي الفرغاني المعروف خان صاحب الفتاوى، تفقه على جماعة من الكبار منهم : أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن علي المرغيناني، وتفقه عليه جماعة من الكبار، منهم: شمس الأئمة محمد بن عبد الستار الكردري، توفي يوم الاثنين خامس عشر رمضان سنة خمس مائة واثنين وتسعين رحمه الله. [رمز الحقائق: ١٩٠/٢] الأشياء الستة والحاصل أن المفتى به التحليف في الكل إلا في الحدود. (ط)] وهي النكاح والرجعة والفيء والرق والنسب والولاء. فإن قلت المذكور تسعة أشياء؟ قلت: قد ذكرنا أن عدم التحليف في الحد واللعان مجمع عليه، فبقيت سبعة، والاستيلاد ملحق بالستة؛ لأن الدعوى فيه دعوى النسب أو دعوى الرق، فتبقى الستة، وهي المختلفة فيها بين الإمام وصاحبيه، واختار الإمام علي البزدوي أيضاً قولهما مثل ما نص عليه القاضي خان، واختار بعض المتأخرين أن القاضي ينظر في حال المدعى عليه، فإن رآه متعنتاً يحلفه آخذاً بقولهما، وإن رآه مظلوماً لا يحلفه آخذاً بقول أبي حنيفة لله [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۹۰/۲] وصورة الاستحلاف على قولهما في النكاح مثلا: ما بزوجة لي وإن كانت زوجة لي فهي طالق بائن؛ لأنها لو كانت صادقة لا يبطل النكاح بجحوده فإذا حلف تبقى معطلة، وقال بعضهم: يستحلف على النكاح فإن حلف بقول القاضي فرقت بينهما. (فتح)
Rulings of Lawsuit. Book of Lawsuit. The judge, Imam Fakhr al-Din, stated that the fatwa is that the denier is made to swear an oath in the six things: the six [categories], and the thief is made to swear an oath; if he refrains, he is liable but not amputated; and the husband when the woman claims... [biography] The six things: and the conclusion is that the mufta bihi is administering the oath in all except in hadd punishments. They are: marriage, revocation, return (fay'), slavery, lineage, and patronage. If you say: nine things are mentioned? I say: we have mentioned that not administering the oath in hadd and li'an is agreed upon, so seven remain, and istilad is attached to the six because the claim therein is a claim of lineage or a claim of slavery, so the six remain, and they are the ones in which there is difference between the Imam and his two companions. Imam Ali al-Bazdawi also chose their opinion as stated by Qadi Khan. Some later scholars chose that the judge looks at the situation of the defendant: if he sees him as obstinate, he administers the oath, taking their opinion; if he sees him as wronged, he does not administer the oath, taking the opinion of Abu Hanifa... The form of administering the oath according to their opinion in marriage, for example: 'By Allah, I have no wife, and if I have a wife, she is divorced irrevocably' because if she were truthful, the marriage would not be invalidated by his denial, so when he swears, she remains suspended. Some said: he is made to swear regarding the marriage; if he swears, according to the judge's statement, a separation is made between them.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa) and immediately states the key ruling: according to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position, the denier (al-munkir) is made to swear an oath only in six specific categories of claims, excluding hudud. These six are: nikah (marriage), raj'ah (revocation of divorce), fay' (return to wife in 'iddah), riq (slavery), nasab (lineage), and wala' (patronage). The text notes that there is a recognized disagreement (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on this rule. Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that no oath is administered to the denier in any of these cases, while the Sahibayn hold that the oath is administered. The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn, as affirmed by Qadi Khan and later scholars such as al-Bazdawi. The text also mentions a third position: a judge may differentiate based on the defendant's behavior—administering the oath if the defendant seems obstinate, but not if he seems wronged. An example is given for marriage: the oath is phrased as 'I have no wife, and if I have one, she is divorced thrice'—this ensures that if the defendant is lying, his oath would itself dissolve the marriage, thus protecting the wife from being stuck in a suspended state. The passage also includes a brief biography of the author, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi al-Farghani, known as Qadi Khan (d. 592 AH).

Key Terms
الأشياء الستة (al-ashya' al-sitta): The six specific categories of claims in which the denier is made to swear an oath: marriage, revocation, return, slavery, lineage, and patronage.
المنكر (al-munkir): The defendant who denies the claim of the plaintiff.
الاستحلاف (al-istihlaf): The act of administering an oath to the defendant in a legal claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this passage, in which of the following is the denier made to swear an oath?
A) Hadd punishment for theft
B) Marriage (nikah)
C) Li'an (mutual imprecation)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi restricts the oath to six specific claims, with a conditional divorce formula to mitigate harm from false oaths, reflecting the school's reliance on istihsan.

The Plaintiff's Right to Demand an Oath with a Present Witness
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oath with present witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a plaintiff can demand an oath when he has a present witness, explain the basis of the disagreement with the Sahibayn, and apply the consensus exceptions.

Core Idea
A plaintiff with a present witness cannot demand an oath—the right to oath is conditioned on inability to produce evidence.

This lesson examines a procedural dispute within the Hanafi school: if the plaintiff claims to have a witness present in the city, can he still demand the defendant's oath? The passage presents Abu Hanifa's view that he cannot, and the Sahibayn's view that he can, along with the hadith evidence and consensus exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Procedural Scenario
The plaintiff says 'I have a present witness' and demands the defendant's oath. The judge must decide whether to administer the oath.
The scenario is when the witness is physically present in the same city (misr), not in the court session.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Its Rationale
Abu Hanifa holds that the oath is not administered because the right to demand an oath is contingent upon the plaintiff's inability to produce evidence. Since he claims to have a witness, he is not incapable.
The rationale: 'thubut haqq al-istihlaf murtab 'ala al-'ajz 'an iqamat al-bayyina'.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Their Dalil
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the oath is administered because the oath is the plaintiff's right regardless of evidence. They cite the hadith of 'Ali: 'You have his oath.'
The hadith: 'lak yaminuhu' – the Sahibayn interpret this as a general right, not conditional.
4
Note the Consensus Cases
If the witness is outside the city, the oath is administered by consensus. If the witness is in the court session, the oath is not administered by consensus. This narrows the dispute.
The ikhtilaf only applies when the witness is present in the city but not in the court.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: when the plaintiff has a present witness, Abu Hanifa denies the oath; the Sahibayn allow it. The judge must choose which view to follow.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated; both views are from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال المدعي: لي بينة حاضرة، وطلب اليمين لم يستحلف، وقيل لخصمه: أعطه كفيلا بنفسك ثلاثة أيام، لم يستحلف عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن ثبوت حق الاستحلاف مرتب على العجز عن إقامة البينة، فلا تكون اليمين حقه دون العجز، وقالا يستحلف؛ لأن اليمين حقه؛ لقوله علي: 'لك يمينه' حين سأل المدعي: ألك بينة؟ فقال: لا، فقال لي: 'لك يمينه، فقال: يحلف ولا يبالي، فقال علي: ليس لك إلا هذا شاهداك أو يمينه'، فللمدعي الاستحلاف إذا طلبه وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا كانت البينة حاضرة في المصر، فإن كانت خارج المصر يحلف بالإجماع، وإن كانت في مجلس الحكم لا يحلف بالإجماع. (عيني، فتح) ثلاثة أيام وهذا استحسان وبه أخذ أبو حنيفة نظراً للمدعي، وليس فيه كثير ضرر بالمدعى عليه؛ لأن الحضور واجب عليه إذا طلبه حتى يعان المدعي على المدعى عليه، ويشخص إلى القاضي، ويحال بينه وبين أشغاله فيصح التكفيل بإحضاره بمجرد الدعوى كاستحلافه. بمجرد الدعوى، والقياس أنه لا يلزمه التكفيل؛ لأن الحق لم يجب عليه بعد بخلاف ما بعد إقامة البيئة. وهذا إذا قال المدعي لي بينة حاضرة، وإن قال: ليس لي بينة أو شهودي غيب، لا يؤخذ منه كفيل؛ لعدم الفائدة في التكفيل؛ لأن الغائب كالهالك من وجه، وليس كل غائب آتيا، ويمكنه الاستحلاف في الحال فلا معنى للاشتغال بالتكفيل. والتقدير بثلاثة أيام هو المروي عن الإمام الأعظم وهو الصحيح، وعن أبي يوسف أنه مقدر بما بين مجلس القاضي حتى إذا كان مجلس القاضي في كل يوم يكفل إلى اليوم الثاني، وإن كان مجلسه في كل عشرة يوماً يكفل إلى عشرة أيام، ولا فرق في ظاهر الرواية بين أن يكون المال
And if the plaintiff says: 'I have a present witness' and demands the oath, he is not made to swear; and it is said to his opponent: 'Give him a surety for your person for three days.' According to Abu Hanifa, he is not made to swear because the right to demand the oath is dependent on inability to produce evidence, so the oath is not his right without inability. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is made to swear because the oath is his right, based on the statement of 'Ali: 'You have his oath' when he asked the plaintiff: 'Do you have evidence?' He said: 'No.' He said to me: 'You have his oath.' He said: 'He swears and does not care.' Then 'Ali said: 'You have nothing except this: your two witnesses or his oath.' So the plaintiff has the right to demand the oath when he requests it. This difference is when the evidence is present in the city; if it is outside the city, he is made to swear by consensus; if it is in the court session, he is not made to swear by consensus. Three days: this is istihsan and Abu Hanifa adopted it in consideration of the plaintiff, and there is no great harm to the defendant because attendance is obligatory upon him when requested, so that the plaintiff is helped against the defendant, and he is brought to the judge, and is prevented from his occupations, so taking a surety for his presence upon mere claim is valid like his oath upon mere claim. By analogy, he would not be required to give a surety because the right has not yet become obligatory, unlike after the establishment of evidence. This is when the plaintiff says 'I have a present witness'; if he says 'I have no evidence' or 'my witnesses are absent', no surety is taken from him because there is no benefit in taking a surety; because the absent one is like a ruined thing in one respect, and not every absent one returns, and he can demand the oath immediately, so there is no meaning to occupying with a surety. The estimation of three days is narrated from the greatest Imam and it is the correct one. From Abu Yusuf that it is estimated by the period between the judge's sessions: if the judge holds court every day, the surety is for the next day; if every ten days, for ten days. And there is no difference in the apparent narration whether the property...
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage discusses a procedural issue: if the plaintiff says he has a witness present (baiyina hadira) but also demands that the defendant be made to swear an oath, can the judge administer the oath? According to Abu Hanifa, the answer is no, because the right to demand an oath is conditioned on the plaintiff's inability to produce evidence; since he claims to have a witness, he is not considered incapable, and therefore he cannot demand an oath. The Sahibayn disagree: they hold that the oath is a right of the plaintiff independently, based on the hadith of 'Ali (RA) where the Prophet instructed a plaintiff who had no evidence to accept the defendant's oath; the Sahibayn interpret this as giving the plaintiff a right to demand the oath whenever he wishes, regardless of evidence availability. The text notes that this ikhtilaf applies only when the witness is present in the city (misr); if the witness is outside the city, the oath is administered by consensus, and if the witness is actually in the court session, the oath is not administered by consensus. The passage then addresses another related issue: when the plaintiff says he has a present witness, the judge orders the defendant to provide a surety (kafil) for his own person for three days, to ensure he will appear when the witness is brought. This is a ruling of istihsan (juristic preference) adopted by Abu Hanifa, out of consideration for the plaintiff. The analogy (qiyas) would suggest no surety is needed because the defendant's obligation is not yet established, but istihsan requires it. The period of three days is the reported view of Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf says it depends on the frequency of the judge's sessions. The text ends incomplete.

Key Terms
البينة الحاضرة (al-bayyina al-hadira): A witness or evidence that is present in the city and can be brought to court.
الكفيل (al-kafil): A surety who guarantees the defendant's appearance in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the plaintiff not allowed to demand an oath when he has a present witness?
A) Because the defendant has the right to refuse
B) Because the right to oath depends on inability to produce evidence
C) Because the judge lacks jurisdiction
D) Because the plaintiff is lying

Key Takeaway
The right to demand an oath is conditioned on the plaintiff's inability to produce evidence; a present witness negates this right according to Abu Hanifa.

The Defendant's Surety When the Plaintiff Claims a Present Witness
Ruling on surety by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the defendant must provide a surety for three days when the plaintiff claims a present witness, explain the istihsan basis, and contrast it with qiyas.

Core Idea
By istihsan, the defendant must give a surety for three days when the plaintiff claims a present witness, even though the obligation is not yet proven.

This lesson covers a procedural ruling of istihsan: when the plaintiff says he has a present witness, the judge orders the defendant to provide a surety for three days to ensure his appearance. The passage explains why this is preferred over qiyas, which would not require a surety, and discusses the duration of the surety according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Trigger
When the plaintiff says 'I have a present witness', the judge tells the defendant: 'Give him a surety for your person for three days.' This is the ruling.
The surety is taken at the stage of mere claim, before evidence is established.
2
Understand the Istihsan Basis
The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) out of consideration for the plaintiff, so that he is helped against the defendant and the defendant does not flee.
The reason: 'nazaran lil mudda'i' and because attendance is obligatory upon the defendant when requested.
3
Contrast with Qiyas
By qiyas, no surety would be required because the defendant's obligation (the right of the plaintiff) has not yet been established—unlike after the evidence is presented.
The qiyas is based on the principle that a surety is only valid when a right is proven.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Difference on Duration
According to Abu Hanifa, the surety is for three days (marwi and sahih). According to Abu Yusuf, it is for the period between the judge's sessions; if court is daily, one day; if every ten days, ten days.
The text states that three days is the correct (sahih) view from the Imam.
5
Apply the Exceptions
If the plaintiff says 'I have no evidence' or 'my witnesses are absent', no surety is taken because there is no benefit—the absent witness may never come, and the plaintiff can demand the oath immediately.
This shows the surety is specifically tied to the claim of a present witness.

The Surety for the Defendant When the Plaintiff Claims a Present Witness
Ruling on surety for defendant when plaintiff claims present witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling requiring the defendant to give a surety when the plaintiff claims a present witness, explain the istihsan reasoning, and identify the intra-Hanafi differences on the oath and surety period.

Core Idea
When plaintiff claims a present witness, defendant gives surety, not an oath—istihsan overrides qiyas.

In a lawsuit, the plaintiff may demand an oath from the defendant to prove his claim. But what if the plaintiff says he has a witness present? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the Hanafi ruling: the defendant is not made to swear; instead, he must provide a surety for three days. This istihsan ruling balances the plaintiff's need to secure attendance with the defendant's procedural rights. We will also examine the internal Hanafi debate about when the oath can be demanded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the procedural scenario
The plaintiff says 'I have a present witness' and demands the defendant to swear an oath. Identify the act: the plaintiff is claiming a right and asserting he has a witness available in the city.
The witness is present 'in the city', not in the court. If the witness were in court, the ruling would differ.
2
Apply the Hanafi ruling on the surety
According to Abu Hanifa, the defendant is not made to swear. Instead, he is told to give a surety (kafil) for three days. The surety must be trustworthy and from the city. This is the mufta bihi position.
The three-day period is from Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf ties it to court sessions.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
The qiyas would say no surety is required because no right is established. But istihsan considers that attendance is obligatory upon the defendant, and the surety is a minimal harm that assists the plaintiff. Identify the effective cause (illa) comparison.
The istihsan overrides qiyas due to practical benefit: 'attendance is obligatory, so surety is a precaution'.
4
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the oath
Abu Hanifa says the plaintiff cannot demand the oath because his claim of a present witness shows ability to produce evidence. The Sahibayn say he can, citing the hadith of Ali. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, surety; under Sahibayn, oath.
This difference applies only when the witness is in the city; if outside, agreement on oath is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال المدعي: لي بينة حاضرة، أي المدعي من خصمه وطلب اليمين لم يستحلف، وقيل لخصمه: أعطه كفيلا بنفسك ثلاثة أيام، أي المدعى عليه أي لخصم المدعي ثقة يؤمن هروبه أي في المصر قبل الوطء بأن قالت: "طلقتني قبل أن تدخل بي" وهذا بالإجماع؛ لأن فيه دعوى المال، وقيد "قبل الوطء" اتفاقي؛ لأن الاستحلاف يجري في الطلاق مطلقاً اتفاقاً. (ط) عيني) ضمن نصف المهر: لأنه يثبت بالطلاق قبل الدخول. (عيني) وجاحد: أي ويستحلف أيضاً منكر القصاص بأن ادعى عليه رجل قصاصاً وهو ينكر؛ لأنه حق العباد (عيني) في النفس أي في قتلها فلا قصاص ولا دية ولكن حبس. (ط) وفيما دونه: أي وإن نكل فيما دون النفس كاليد والرجل. (معدن) يقتص: بنكوله عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن النكول بذل، وإنما يجوز في الطرف ولا يجوز في النفس، ألا ترى أنه لو قتله بأمره يجب عليه القصاص في رواية ولو قطع يده بأمره لا يجب عليه الأرش إعمالاً للبذل إلا أنه لا يباح فيأثم، وفي كيفية الاستحلاف على القتل روايتان في رواية: يستحلف على الحاصل بالله ما له علي دم ولا دم، وفي رواية: يستحلف على السبب: بالله ما قتلت فلان بن فلان وعندهما يلزمه الدية فيهما ولا يقضى بالقصاص؛ لأن النكول إقرار، فيصح لإيجاب المال دون القصاص، وعند الثلاثة يقتص فيهما بعد حلف المدعي. [رمز الحقائق: ١٩١/٢] لم يستحلف عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن ثبوت حق الاستحلاف مرتب على العجز عن إقامة البينة، فلا تكون اليمين حقه دون العجز، وقالا يستحلف؛ لأن اليمين حقه؛ لقوله علي: "لك يمينه" حين سأل المدعي: ألك بينة؟ فقال: لا، فقال لي: "لك يمينه، فقال: يحلف ولا يبالي، فقال علي: ليس لك إلا هذا شاهداك أو يمينه"، فللمدعي الاستحلاف إذا طلبه وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا كانت البينة حاضرة في المصر، فإن كانت خارج المصر يحلف بالإجماع، وإن كانت في مجلس الحكم لا يحلف بالإجماع. (عيني، فتح) ثلاثة أيام وهذا استحسان وبه أخذ أبو حنيفة نظراً للمدعي، وليس فيه كثير ضرر بالمدعى عليه؛ لأن الحضور واجب عليه إذا طلبه حتى يعان المدعي على المدعى عليه، ويشخص إلى القاضي، ويحال بينه وبين أشغاله فيصح التكفيل بإحضاره بمجرد الدعوى كاستحلافه. بمجرد الدعوى، والقياس أنه لا يلزمه التكفيل؛ لأن الحق لم يجب عليه بعد بخلاف ما بعد إقامة البيئة. وهذا إذا قال المدعي لي بينة حاضرة، وإن قال: ليس لي بينة أو شهودي غيب، لا يؤخذ منه كفيل؛ لعدم الفائدة في التكفيل؛ لأن الغائب كالهالك من وجه، وليس كل غائب آتيا، ويمكنه الاستحلاف في الحال فلا معنى للاشتغال بالتكفيل. والتقدير بثلاثة أيام هو المروي عن الإمام الأعظم وهو الصحيح، وعن أبي يوسف أنه مقدر بما بين مجلس القاضي حتى إذا كان مجلس القاضي في كل يوم يكفل إلى اليوم الثاني، وإن كان مجلسه في كل عشرة يوماً يكفل إلى عشرة أيام، ولا فرق في ظاهر الرواية بين أن يكون المال .

فإن أبي لازمه أي دار معه حيث سار ولو غريبا لازمه قدر مجلس القاضي الغريم . . . (عيني، فتح مجلس القاضي وكذا لا يكفل إلا إلى آخر المجلس. (عيني)
وعن محمد: أن المدعى عليه إن كان معروفاً وجيهاً يعلم أن مثله لا يخفي نفسه بذلك القدر من المال، لا يجبر على إعطاء الكفيل [رمز الحقائق: ١٩١/٢] فإن أبي: أي امتنع المدعى عليه عن إعطاء الكفيل. (معدن) حيث سار : أي الغريم مقدار مدة التكفيل حتى لا يغيب. (ط، عيني) ولو غريباً : أي لو كان المدعى عليه مسافراً. (عيني) لازمه إلخ : أي لازمه بنفسه أو أمينه إلى أن يقوم القاضي من مجلسه؛ لأنه يلحقه الضرر بالزيادة على ذلك، حتى لو علم القاضي وقت سفره، يكفل إليه، وينظر في زيه، ويستخبر رفقائه عن سفره لو أنكره المدعي وللمدعي أن يطلب وكيلاً بالخصومة حتى لو غاب الأصيل يقيم البينة على الأصيل، وإن أعطاه وكيلاً له أن يطالبه بالكفيل بنفس الوكيل، وإن أعطاه كفيلاً بنفس الوكيل، له أن يطالبه بالكفيل بنفس الأصيل لو كان المدعى ديناً، وإن كان المدعى منقولاً، له أن يطلب منه . ذلك كفيلاً بالعين ليحضرها، وإن كان عقاراً لا يحتاج على ذلك؛ لأنه لا يقبل التغييب. أن يكون الواحد كفيلاً بالنفس ووكيلاً بالخصومة؛ لأن الواحد يقوم بهما، ويشترط في الوكيل ما يشترط في الكفيل بأن يكون ثقة معروف الدار، وقيل: أن يكون له دار وحانوت ملكاً له، وقيل: أن يكون ثقة بوظائفه بالأوقاف؛ لأنه لا يتركها ويهرب، ولا يكون لجوجا معروفاً بالخصومة، ويكون من أهل المصر لا غريباً، والحاصل: وصح أن المدار على الأمن من الهروب. (عيني، فتح مجلس القاضي وكذا لا يكفل إلا إلى آخر المجلس. (عيني)
And if the plaintiff says: 'I have a present witness,' meaning the plaintiff from his opponent and demands the oath, he is not made to swear. And it is said to his opponent: 'Give him a surety for yourself for three days,' meaning the defendant, i.e., to the opponent of the plaintiff, a trustworthy person whose flight is safe, i.e., in the city. Before intercourse, as when she says: 'You divorced me before you entered upon me,' and this is by consensus because it involves a claim of property. The restriction 'before intercourse' is by agreement because the oath runs in divorce absolutely by agreement. (T, Ayni) He guarantees half the dower because it is established by divorce before entry. (Ayni) And the denier of retaliation: meaning he is also made to swear against the denier of retaliation when a man claims retaliation against him and he denies it, because it is a right of the servants. (Ayni) In the soul, meaning in killing it, so no retaliation and no blood money but imprisonment. (T) And in what is less than it: meaning if he refuses the oath in what is less than the soul, like the hand and foot. (Maden) He is retaliated against by his nukul according to Abu Hanifa because nukul is a surrender, and it is only permissible in limbs and not in the soul. Do you not see that if he killed him by his command, retaliation would be obligatory in one narration; and if he cut off his hand by his command, the compensation is not obligatory, acting upon the surrender, except that it is not permissible and he sins. And regarding the manner of the oath on killing, there are two narrations: in one narration, he swears on the outcome: 'By Allah, I owe him no blood and no blood'; in another narration, he swears on the cause: 'By Allah, I did not kill so-and-so son of so-and-so.' And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the blood money is obliged in both cases and qisas is not decreed because nukul is an admission, so it is valid for imposing financial liability but not for qisas. And according to the three (Abu Hanifa and the two?) retaliation is exacted in both after the plaintiff's oath. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 191/2] He is not made to swear according to Abu Hanifa because the establishment of the right to swear is dependent on inability to produce evidence, so the oath is not his right without inability. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is made to swear because the oath is his right, based on the statement of Ali: 'You have his oath' when the plaintiff asked: 'Do you have evidence?' He said: 'No.' He said to me: 'You have his oath.' He said: 'He swears and does not care.' Ali said: 'You have nothing except this: your two witnesses or his oath.' So the plaintiff has the right to have him swear if he demands it. This difference is when the witness is present in the city. If it is outside the city, he swears by consensus; if it is in the court, he does not swear by consensus. (Ayni, Fath) Three days, and this is istihsan and Abu Hanifa adopted it out of consideration for the plaintiff. There is not much harm to the defendant because attendance is obligatory upon him when requested, so that the plaintiff is assisted against the defendant, and he is brought to the judge and prevented from his affairs. So taking a surety for his presence is valid upon mere claim, like his oath upon mere claim. The qiyas is that he is not obliged to provide surety because the right has not yet been established against him, unlike after evidence is presented. This is if the plaintiff says: 'I have a present witness.' If he says: 'I have no witness' or 'my witnesses are absent,' no surety is taken from him because there is no benefit in the surety, as the absent one is like a dead person in one sense, and not every absent person returns. He can be made to swear immediately, so there is no point in engaging in surety. The estimation of three days is that which is narrated from the Great Imam and it is the correct opinion. According to Abu Yusuf, it is estimated by the time between court sessions: if the court sits every day, he gives surety until the next day; if it sits every ten days, he gives surety for ten days. There is no difference in the apparent narration whether the property is large or small, or whether the defendant is obscure or prominent, or the like. According to Muhammad: if the defendant is known to be prominent and it is known that someone like him would not hide himself for that amount of property, he is not forced to give a surety. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 191/2] If he refuses: meaning if the defendant refuses to give the surety, he is accompanied wherever he goes, even if he is a traveler, for the duration of the surety period until the judge rises from his session. (Ayni, Fath) The meaning of 'wherever he goes' is that the debtor (defendant) is accompanied for the duration of the surety period so that he does not disappear. (T, Ayni) 'Even if a stranger' means if the defendant is a traveler. (Ayni) 'He accompanies him, etc.' means he accompanies him in person or by his deputy until the judge rises from his session, because he would suffer harm by exceeding that. Even if the judge knows the time of his travel, he gives surety up to that time; he examines his attire and inquires about his travel companions if the plaintiff denies his travel. The plaintiff may request a proxy for litigation, so that if the principal is absent, he can present evidence against the principal. If he gives a proxy, he can demand surety from the proxy himself. If he gives a surety from the proxy, he can demand surety from the principal himself if the claim is for a debt. If the claim is for a movable, he may demand a surety for the specific item to be produced. If it is immovable, he does not need that because it cannot be hidden. One person can be both a surety for the person and a proxy for litigation, as one person can undertake both. The conditions for the proxy are the same as for the surety: he must be trustworthy, with a known residence. Some say he must have a house and shop owned by him. Some say he must be trustworthy with his positions in awqaf because he would not leave them and flee. He should not be litigious or known for litigation. He should be from the city's inhabitants, not a stranger. The bottom line: the criterion is security from flight. (Ayni, Fath) Likewise, surety is only given until the end of the court session. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Da'wa (Book of Claims) addressing the procedure when a plaintiff claims to have a present witness and demands an oath from the defendant. The text presents the ruling, the reasoning (istihsan vs. qiyas), and intra-Hanafi differences.

The author begins by stating that if the plaintiff says 'I have a present witness' and demands the oath, the defendant is not made to swear immediately. Instead, the defendant is told to provide a surety (kafil) for himself for three days. This surety must be a trustworthy person whose flight is not feared, and he must be from the city.

The text then digresses into related rulings: in a divorce claim before consummation, the oath leads to payment of half the mahr upon nukul (refusal to swear). In retaliation claims (qisas), the denier is made to swear; if he refuses (nukul), for claims involving life he is imprisoned until he admits or swears, but for limbs, qisas is imposed by nukul according to Abu Hanifa. The commentary explains that nukul is treated as a surrender (badhl), so it is valid for imposing financial obligations but not for qisas in life. There is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two (Sahibayn) on the effect of nukul: according to them, nukul is an admission that imposes blood money but not qisas. The three (Abu Hanifa and others?) say qisas is imposed after the plaintiff swears.

Returning to the main issue: Abu Hanifa holds that the defendant is not made to swear when the plaintiff claims to have a present witness, because the right to demand the oath is conditional on inability to produce evidence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is made to swear, citing the hadith of Ali. This difference applies only when the witness is in the city; if outside, the defendant is made to swear by consensus; if in the court, he is not.

The ruling of the three-day surety is istihsan (juristic preference) adopted by Abu Hanifa out of consideration for the plaintiff. The qiyas would be that no surety is required because no right has been established. The condition for this is that the plaintiff actually says he has a witness present; if he says he has no witness or his witnesses are absent, no surety is taken. The three-day period is narrated from Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf says it depends on the court session interval. Muhammad adds that if the defendant is known to be prominent and unlikely to flee for such a small amount, he is not forced to give a surety.

If the defendant refuses to give a surety, he is accompanied (arrested or followed) for the duration of the surety period, even if he is a traveler. The accompaniment is limited to the court session time to avoid undue hardship. The plaintiff may also request a proxy for litigation. Conditions for the proxy and surety are discussed: they must be trustworthy, with a known residence, not litigious, and from the city. The overriding principle is security from flight.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yamin): The oath taken by the defendant in a lawsuit, a procedural right to establish or deny a claim.
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath after it is offered to him, which is treated as an admission of the claim.
الكفيل (al-kafil): A surety who guarantees the defendant's presence in court for a specified period.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in order to achieve a more equitable outcome, used here to require the surety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling when a plaintiff says 'I have a present witness' and demands the oath from the defendant?
A) The defendant is made to swear immediately.
B) The defendant must provide a surety for three days.
C) The plaintiff must bring the witness before any other action.
D) The case is dismissed until the witness appears.

Key Takeaway
When a plaintiff claims a present witness, the defendant is not made to swear but must provide a surety for three days, based on istihsan overriding qiyas.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Manner of Oath in Litigation: By Allah Alone
Ruling with proof on the valid oath in litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the valid oath is by Allah, explain why oaths by divorce or emancipation are prohibited, and identify the exceptional case when they may be used.

Core Idea
An oath in court is only valid by Allah; swearing by divorce or emancipation is haram, except to compel an obstinate litigant.

In this lesson, we examine the proper manner of the oath in litigation. Based on clear hadith, the Hanafi school establishes that the only permissible and valid oath is one sworn by Allah Almighty. Swearing by divorce or emancipation is prohibited and considered sinful. However, there is a narrow exception: if a litigant is obstinate and does not fear an oath by Allah, the judge may make him swear by divorce or emancipation as a compulsion. Even then, if he refuses, no adverse judgment is passed because he is refraining from what is prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the oath (yamin) in litigation. The ruling is that the valid oath is by Allah; oaths by divorce or emancipation are prohibited (haram).
The text also mentions equality of persons: free/slave, man/woman.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs cited: hadith from Ibn Umar (Bukhari, Muslim), Abu Hurairah (Nasai), and Ibn Mas'ud. Also the statement 'Cursed is he who swears by divorce'.
The hadith explicitly command swearing by Allah or remaining silent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these hadith prove the ruling? The imperative 'let him swear by Allah or remain silent' (falyahlif billah aw li yasmut) shows that the only permissible oath is by Allah. The prohibition 'do not swear except by Allah' reinforces this. The curse on swearing by divorce shows its severe prohibition.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the command indicates obligation) applies here.
4
Note the exception
The author states an exception: if the opponent is persistently obstinate (alhha al-khasm) and does not care about an oath by Allah, then the judge may make him swear by divorce or emancipation.
This is a procedural concession based on necessity.
5
Analyze the consequence of refusal
If the defendant refuses to swear by divorce, no judgment is passed against him (nukul) because he is refraining from what is prohibited.
This protects the defendant from being penalized for disobeying a sinful command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واليمين بالله تعالى: [أي اليمين المعتبر أن يحلف بالله والحر والمملوك والرجل والمرأة في اليمين سواء. (ط، عيني)] وفي النسخة التي شرحها العيني هنا "فصل"، وكتب العيني تحته في كيفية اليمين والاستحلاف" ولم يوجد "فصل" في غيرها، ولما فرغ المصنف من ذكر نفس اليمين والمواضع الواجبة هي فيها ذكر صفتها، أي اليمين المشروع المعتبر بالله تعالى، لما روى ابن الله أنه سمع عمر الله وهو يحلف بأبيه، فقال: "إن الله ينهاكم أن تحلفوا بآبائكم، فمن كان حالفاً، فليحلف بالله، أو ليصمت"، رواه البخاري ومسلم وأحمد، وعن أبي هريرة له قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا تحلفوا إلا بالله، ولا تحلفوا إلا وأنتم صادقون"، رواه النسائي، وعن ابن مسعود له: لأن أحلف بالله كاذباً خير من أن أحلف بغيره صادقاً. [رمز الحقائق: ١٩٢/٢]
لا بطلاق وعتاق: أي لا يكون اليمين معتبراً بطلاق؛ لقوله عليه: "ملعون من حلف بالطلاق"، فالتحليف بهما حرام، بل اختلفوا في كفره. إذا ألح الخصم بأن كان لجوجاً متعنتاً لا يبالي باليمين بالله. (ع)] فحينئذ يحلف بالطلاق أو العتاق أو بهما، لكن إذا نكل المدعى عليه عن الحلف بالطلاق لا يقضى عليه بالنكول؛ لأنه امتنع عما هو منهي
And the oath is by Allah, the Exalted: [i.e., the valid oath is that one swears by Allah; the free and the slave, the man and the woman are equal in the oath. (T, Ayni)] In the copy that al-Ayni commented on, here there is 'Fasl', and al-Ayni wrote under it 'On the manner of the oath and the swearing'; but 'Fasl' is not found in other copies. When the author finished mentioning the oath itself and the places where it is obligatory, he mentioned its description, i.e., the legislated valid oath is by Allah, the Exalted, based on what Ibn Umar narrated that he heard Umar swearing by his father, so he said: 'Indeed, Allah forbids you to swear by your fathers. So whoever is swearing, let him swear by Allah or remain silent.' Narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and Ahmad. And from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not swear except by Allah, and do not swear except when you are truthful.' Narrated by al-Nasa'i. And from Ibn Mas'ud: 'That I swear by Allah falsely is better than that I swear by other than Allah truthfully.' [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 192/2]
Not by divorce and emancipation: i.e., the oath is not valid by divorce, because of his saying: 'Cursed is he who swears by divorce.' So making someone swear by them is prohibited; indeed, they differed on its disbelief. When the opponent is persistent, being litigious and obstinate, not caring about the oath by Allah. (A) Then in that case he swears by divorce or emancipation or both. But if the defendant refuses (nukul) from swearing by divorce, no judgment is passed against him for nukul because he refrained from what is prohibited.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage addresses the manner of the oath (al-yamin) in litigation. The author establishes that the only valid and legitimate oath is one sworn by Allah Almighty. This is supported by multiple hadith: the Prophet forbade swearing by one's fathers, commanded swearing by Allah or remaining silent, and prohibited swearing except by Allah. The equality of free and slave, man and woman in the oath is noted.

Critically, the author states that oaths by divorce (talaq) or emancipation (itaq) are not recognized as valid oaths. In fact, swearing by them is prohibited (haram), and some scholars even consider it kufr (disbelief). The basis is the prophetic curse on one who swears by divorce.

However, an exception is made: if the opponent (the person being asked to swear) is persistently obstinate (alhha al-khasm) and does not care about an oath by Allah, then the judge may make him swear by divorce or emancipation. This is a procedural concession to compel a recalcitrant litigant. But if the defendant refuses to swear by divorce, no consequence of nukul (refusal) is applied, because he is refraining from something that is prohibited—his refusal is not treated as an admission.

The passage thus clarifies the normative ruling and the exceptional circumstances.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yamin): The solemn oath sworn by the litigant, which must be by Allah to be valid.
الطلاق (al-talaq): Divorce; used as an oath form (e.g., 'if I did X, my wife is divorced'), but such oaths are prohibited in court.
العتاق (al-itaq): Emancipation; similar to talaq, used as an oath form and treated the same way.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on swearing by divorce or emancipation in court?
A) It is the preferred way to swear.
B) It is permissible in all cases.
C) It is prohibited (haram), but may be used if the opponent is persistently obstinate.
D) It is valid only if the opponent agrees.

Key Takeaway
An oath in court is only valid by Allah; swearing by divorce or emancipation is prohibited, but may be used to compel an obstinate litigant.

Qada — Judiciary

The Manner of Oath in Hanafi Legal Procedure
Describes the manner of oath and its conditions in Hanafi legal procedure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the valid form of oath, distinguish between permissible and impermissible intensifications, and apply the rules to Muslim and non-Muslim litigants.

Core Idea
The oath in Hanafi fiqh must be by Allah alone; swearing by divorce or manumission is forbidden and legally invalid.

The oath (al-yamin) is a critical procedural tool in Islamic courts to resolve claims when evidence is lacking. This lesson examines the Hanafi rules on how an oath is administered: what wording is valid, what intensifications are allowed, and how to handle non-Muslim litigants. The source text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq provides the core rulings supported by hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the oath administered by the judge to the defendant. The ruling: it must be by Allah alone, not by divorce or manumission.
This is the foundational rule.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites hadiths from Ibn 'Umar, Abu Hurayra, and Ibn Mas'ud forbidding oaths by other than Allah and commanding to swear by Allah.
These hadiths are ahad but have qat'i dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyahlif bi Allah' indicates obligation; the prohibition of swearing by fathers implies prohibition of all non-Allah oaths.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on taghliz
Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali allow intensification by time/place; Hanafi restricts to attributes only.
The Hanafi argument: adding time/place is an unauthorized increase (zayd ala al-nass).
5
Apply the ruling to non-Muslims
Jews and Christians swear by Allah who revealed their scripture; others (non-scriptuary) swear by Allah alone without additional references.
There is intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

لا بطلاق وعتاق: أي لا يكون اليمين معتبراً بطلاق؛ لقوله عليه: "ملعون من حلف بالطلاق"، فالتحليف بهما حرام، بل اختلفوا في كفره. إذا ألح الخصم بأن كان لجوجاً متعنتاً لا يبالي باليمين بالله. بذكر أوصافه [أي بذكر أوصاف الله بدون حرف العطف؛ لئلا تكرر اليمين (معدن)] مثل أن يقول: بالله الذي لا إله إلا هو عالم الغيب والشهادة، هو الرحمن الرحيم الذي يعلم من السر، ويعلم من العلانية ما لفلان هذا علي ولا قبلي هذا المال الذي ادعاه، وهو كذا وكذا، وإنما تغلظ بذكر الأوصاف؛ لأن منهم من يمتنع عن اليمين بالتغليظ ويتجاسر عند عدمه فيغلظ عليه لعله يمتنع بذلك، ولو لم يغلظ جاز، وقيل: لا يغلظ على الإنسان المعروف بالصلاح ويغلظ على غيره، وقيل : يغلظ في الخطير من المال دون الحقير 
فلو غلظ فحلف من غير تغليظ ونكل التغليظ لا يقضى عليه بالنكول؛ لأن المقصود الحلف بالله وقد حصل، وفيما إذا غلظ بذكر الصفة يحترز عن الإتيان بالواو لئلا يتكرر اليمين. (فتح)
بعده عن لا بزمان ومكان: أي لا تغلظ اليمين على المسلم بزمان ومكان مطلقاً؛ لأن في التغليظ بالزمان تأخير حق المدعي في اليمين إلى ذلك الزمان وكذا بالمكان؛ لأن فيه التأخير إلى الوصول إلى ذلك المكان المغلظ به فلا يشرع. وظاهر "الهداية": أن المنفي وجوب التغليظ فيكون مشروعاً، وفي "المحيط": ما يدل على إباحته ولكن ذكر أنه لا يجوز التغليظ بالمكان، وقال الشافعي: إن كان اليمين في قسامة أو لعان أو في مال عظيم يبلغ مائتي مثقال يغلظ بالمكان، فيحلف بين الركن والمقام إن كان بمكة، وعند قبر النبي عليه إن كان في المدينة، وعند الصخرة إن كان في بيت المقدس، وفي الجامع إن كان في غيرها، وإن لم يكن الجامع ففي المساجد ويكون ذلك الجمعة بعد العصر، وبه قال مالك وأحمد في رواية ولنا: إطلاق قوله علي: "اليمين على من أنكر"، والتخصيص بالزمان أو المكان زيادة على النص، وهو نسخ.
ويستحلف اليهودي ولا يحلف بالإشارة إلى مصحف معين بأن يقول: بالله الذي أنزل هذا التوراة، أو هذا الإنجيل؛ لأنه يثبت تحريف بعضها، فلا يؤمن أن تقع الإشارة إلى الحرف المحرف فيكون التحليف به تعظيماً لما ليس من كلام وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه لا يحلف أحداً من أهل الكفر إلا بالله تعالى خالصاً؛ احترازاً عن إشراك غيره وذكر الخصاف: أنه لا يحلف غير اليهودي والنصراني إلا بالله، وهو اختيار بعض مشائخنا؛ لأن ذكر النار مع اسم الله تعالى تعظيم لها، ولا ينبغي أن تعظم، بخلاف الكتابيين؛ لأن كتب الله تعالى معظمة، وانظر بما إذا يستحلف الدهري؛ لأنه لا يعتقد وجوده تعالى.
الله
بالتعظيم مع الله،
Book of Claims. Manner of oath and administering oath. If he refuses, he shall be imprisoned with him wherever he goes, even if he is a stranger, for the duration of the judge's session. The oath is by Allah Almighty, not by divorce or manumission, unless the opponent is obstinate. ... The oath by Allah Almighty: i.e., the valid oath is to swear by Allah, and free and slave, man and woman are equal in oath. ... Not by divorce and manumission: i.e., the oath is not considered by divorce due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Cursed is he who swears by divorce.' So administering oath by them is forbidden; rather, they differed regarding its disbelief. ... By mentioning His attributes: i.e., by mentioning the attributes of Allah without the conjunction, so that the oath is not repeated. ... Not by time and place: i.e., the oath is not intensified for the Muslim by time and place absolutely. ... And the Jew is made to swear: by Allah who revealed the Torah to Moses, and the Christian by Allah who revealed the Gospel to Jesus.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the manner of administering oaths in legal claims. It begins with the ruling that if a defendant refuses to provide a surety (kafil), the judge may imprison him until the end of the session. The details are explained: if the defendant is a stranger, he is detained only for the session; the judge may investigate his travel plans. The core of the lesson is that the oath must be by Allah alone, not by divorce or manumission, as these are forbidden and even considered disbelief. The text provides hadith evidence. It then discusses intensification (taghliz) of the oath: it is done by mentioning Allah's attributes, but not by specifying a time or place, contrary to Shafi'i and others who allow it in certain cases. Finally, it addresses oaths of non-Muslims: a Jew swears by Allah who revealed the Torah, a Christian by Allah who revealed the Gospel. There is a difference of opinion whether to mention specific scriptures due to corruption. The Hanafi position is to keep the oath purely by Allah.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yamin): The oath sworn by the defendant in a legal claim to deny the plaintiff's allegation.
التغليظ (al-taghliz): Intensification of the oath by adding attributes of Allah to increase its solemnity.
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal to take the oath, which may result in a judgment against the refuser.
الاستحلاف (al-istihlaf): The act of administering an oath by the judge to the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on intensifying the oath by mentioning a specific time or place?
A) Permitted in all cases.
B) Permitted only if the defendant agrees.
C) Not permitted at all.
D) Permitted only for non-Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The valid oath in Hanafi law is solely by Allah's name; any other form (divorce, manumission) or unnecessary intensifications are invalid.

Administering Oaths to Magians and Idol Worshippers
Ruling on oath forms and location for non-Muslim litigants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi oath formulas for a Magian and an idol worshipper, explain why oaths are not taken in their places of worship, and apply the ruling to a non-Muslim litigant scenario.

Core Idea
Oaths are tailored to each litigant's belief; the judge must administer them accordingly and never in their places of worship.

In a Hanafi court, when a non-Muslim litigant is required to take an oath, the formula must be customized to their religious beliefs. This ensures the oath is taken seriously and respects Islamic legal principles. This lesson presents the specific rulings for Magians (fire-worshippers) and idol worshippers, along with procedural restrictions regarding the location of the oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of non-Muslim litigants
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between a Majusi (Magian/Zoroastrian) and a Wathani (idol worshipper). The former venerates fire, the latter worships other beings but still believes in God.
These are not the only non-Muslim categories; the ruling is specific to these two.
2
State the oath formula for each
For the Magian, the oath is 'by Allah who created the fire'; for the idol worshipper, it is simply 'by Allah' without any addition. The principle is to emphasize what the litigant venerates or to avoid mentioning what they associate.
The Magian's oath mentions the Creator of fire to distance him from fire-worship.
3
Note the prohibition of swearing in their places of worship
Oaths are not to be administered in churches, synagogues, or fire temples because the judge is prohibited from entering them, and doing so would involve veneration of places where falsehood is practiced.
The judge must administer the oath in the court or another permissible location.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The oath is made severe ('taghliz') according to what the litigant believes. This principle ensures that the oath is binding and taken seriously by the swearer.
This is a key maxim in Hanafi judicial procedure.
5
Recognize the ruling for Muslims entering such places
It is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi) for a Muslim to enter churches or synagogues, amounting to prohibition. A Muslim who frequents such places with non-Muslims may be subject to discretionary punishment (ta'zir).
This is a separate but related ruling derived from the same passage.

Source Text

And any of these mentioned ones is made to swear by its Creator. The Magian: i.e., the Magian is made to swear, and he is the one who worships fire. The conclusion is that the oath is made severe upon each according to what he believes. (Ma'din) In their places of worship because there is veneration in them, and the judge is prohibited from attending them. ('Ayni)] They are the churches and synagogues; because the judge does not attend them, rather he is prohibited from that. Moreover, for every Muslim it is disliked to enter the synagogue and church because they are gathering places of devils. And evidently the dislike is prohibition. He said in al-Bahr [7/304]: And I have given a fatwa for disciplining a Muslim who frequents the church with the Jews.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on how to administer oaths to non-Muslim litigants in a Hanafi court. The Magian (fire-worshipper) is made to swear by Allah who created the fire, emphasizing the Creator to distance him from his reverence for the fire. The idol worshipper swears by Allah alone, without associating anything, because he still believes in a deity. The key principle: the oath is tailored to what the litigant venerates. Additionally, oaths are not administered in their places of worship (churches, synagogues) because the judge is prohibited from attending them, and for Muslims it is severely disliked (approaching prohibition) to enter such places. This ruling ensures the oath is taken seriously and respects Islamic prohibitions.

Key Terms
مجوسي (majusi): Zoroastrian fire-worshipper; litigant in a Hanafi court.
وثني (wathani): Idol worshipper; one who worships other than Allah but believes in God.
بيعة (bi'ah): Church or synagogue; place of worship for non-Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi procedure, the oath for a non-Muslim litigant must be tailored to their beliefs and taken outside their places of worship, ensuring both effectiveness and compliance with Islamic prohibitions.
